    "the role and physics of accretion in dense ( proto)cluster environments are central to understanding massive star formation , yet remain poorly understood ( c.f . * ? ? ?",
    "this is in part attributable to the rapid evolution of massive young stellar objects ( mysos ) : sources in a phase of active accretion are expected to be rare ( e.g. * ? ? ?",
    "* ) , and are observationally difficult to identify in distant , crowded , and heavily extincted massive star forming regions ( msfrs ) .    the 4.5 @xmath2 m band of the _ spitzer space telescope s _ infrared array camera ( irac , * ? ? ?",
    "* ) offers a promising new approach for identifying mysos with outflows that are , presumably , still actively accreting .",
    "the 4.5 @xmath2 m irac band ( `` band 2 '' ) is notably lacking in pah features ( c.f .",
    "fig . 1 of * ? ? ?",
    "* ) and contains molecular lines that may be shock - excited in protostellar outflows , including both the co ( v=1 - 0 ) bandhead and h@xmath7 lines , most notably the v=0 - 0 , s(9,10,11 ) transitions .",
    "weaker h@xmath7 lines can also , in aggregate , contribute significantly to the 4.5 @xmath2 m broadband flux under some shock conditions , or if photodissociation region ( pdr ) emission is present ( e.g. * ? ? ?",

    "there are also h@xmath7 lines in the other irac bands , and indeed , in the more extreme shock environment of supernova remnants ( snr ) , @xcite have found that all irac bands may be dominated by h@xmath7 emission . in msfrs , however , pah emission generally dominates the 5.8 and 8.0 @xmath2 m bands . thus extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission with morphology distinct from that in the other irac bands is a common and conspicuous feature of msfrs .",
    "such features are known as `` extended green objects ( egos ) '' @xcite or `` green fuzzies '' @xcite , for the common coding of the [ 4.5 ] band as green in three - color irac images . in the massive dr21 outflow ,",

    "@xcite catalogued over 300 egos in the galactic legacy infrared mid - plane survey extraordinaire survey area ( glimpse , * ? ? ?",
    "catalogued egos were divided into `` likely '' and `` possible '' myso outflow candidates based primarily on the angular extent and morphology of the 4.5 @xmath2 m emission @xcite",
    ". egos for which the mir morphology may be attributable to multiple nearby point sources or to image artifacts around bright sources , instead of to truly extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission , were categorized as `` possible '' outflow candidates ( see also * ? ? ?",
    "the glimpse survey is also sensitive to another class of objects identified with the early stages of massive star formation : infrared dark clouds ( irdcs ) , seen in silhouette against mir galactic background emission , particularly at 8 @xmath2 m @xcite .",
    "first identified and catalogued in _ infrared space observatory ( iso ) _ and _ midcourse space experiment ( msx ) _ surveys of the galactic plane , irdcs are cold ( t@xmath820 k ) , dense ( n(h@xmath7)@xmath910@xmath11 @xmath12 ) clouds of molecular gas and dust ( e.g. * ? ? ?",

    "recent studies have shown that irdcs host both protostellar cores and intermediate and massive ysos , pinpointing irdcs as sites of the earliest stages of massive star and cluster formation ( e.g. * ? ? ?",

    "colors of egos and their correlation with irdcs and published 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser data , @xcite argued that egos constitute a population of actively accreting myso outflow candidates .",
    "there are two elements to this hypothesis : ( 1 ) egos are _ massive _ ysos and ( 2 ) extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission traces active molecular outflows from these mysos ( which may then be presumed to be actively accreting ) .",
    "recent advances in the theoretical and observational understanding of ch@xmath0oh masers , particularly the differing conditions under which class i and class ii transitions are excited , suggest that ch@xmath0oh masers are well suited for testing this hypothesis and establishing the nature of egos .",
    "collisionly excited class i ch@xmath0oh masers are observationally well - correlated with molecular outflows in msfrs @xcite . in the largest interferometric survey to date , @xcite found that 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers were common in msfrs and well correlated with shocked gas in outflows as traced by sio and h@xmath7 .",
    "based on the relation of 95 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh maser emission to molecular cores traced by cs and outflow shocks traced by h@xmath7 in dr21 and on the close - to - systemic velocities of the masers ( v@xmath13@xmath1v@xmath14 ) , @xcite suggested that class i ch@xmath0oh masers may be excited specifically in interface regions where outflows encounter surrounding molecular material .",
    "class i ch@xmath0oh masers in several transitions are associated with shocked h@xmath7 knots in the outflow from iras 16547 - 4247 @xcite , a well - studied myso that is also an ego catalogued by @xcite .",
    "@xcite find that 67% of the egos catalogued by @xcite are within 1 of a 44 or 95 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh maser , but that the class i ch@xmath0oh maser data available in the literature  mostly from single dish surveys with poor angular resolution ( @xmath1552@xmath10)is insufficient to establish physical association between the maser and mir emission .",
    "the single dish surveys used by @xcite are also shallow ( detection limits @xmath35 jy ) , and comparison with the @xcite results suggests that shallow surveys miss a substantial fraction of the maser population , at least for 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers .",
    "only @xmath129% of the masers reported by @xcite have peak flux densities @xmath35 jy , although @xmath133% of molinari sources and @xmath159% of all sources with 44 ghz detections are associated with at least one @xmath35 jy maser . there is evidence that relatively weak ( @xmath1611 jy ) 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers can occur in bipolar outflows from low - mass protostars @xcite , but the authors caution that the maser nature of the observed emission requires confirmation with interferometric observations .",

    "in addition to being an observationally robust result , the lack of 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers towards low - mass ysos may be understood theoretically in the context of the excitation models : the energetics of low - mass ysos do not produce regions with the necessary combinations of dust temperature , density , and ch@xmath0oh abundance for 6.7 ghz maser emission @xcite .",
    "unaffected by extinction and accessible at high angular resolution with the expanded very large array ( evla ) , 6.7 ghz class ii and 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers provide an observationally efficient avenue for testing whether egos are massive ysos with outflows .",
    "this paper presents the results of a survey for 6.7 ghz class ii and 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers towards a sample of @xmath120 egos selected from the catalog of @xcite , chosen to cover a range of mir properties and be visible from the northern hemisphere .",
    "we also report results from simultaneous evla 44 ghz psuedo - continuum observations and from a james clerk maxwell telescope ( jcmt ) molecular line survey undertaken to complement the maser observations by providing information about the gas kinematics and lsr velocities . in ",
    "[ obs ] we describe the observations , in  [ results ] we present the results of the surveys , in  [ discussion ] we discuss the implications of our results for understanding the nature of egos , and in  5 we summarize our main conclusions .",
    "the 6.7 ghz observations reported here were made possible by the expanded tuning capability of the nrao expanded very large array ( evla ) at c band .",
    "a sample of 28 egos was initially observed in the 6.668519 ghz ch@xmath0oh ( 5@xmath19 - 6@xmath20 )  a@xmath4 ( @xmath21=48.7 k ) maser transition on 2007 october 31 in the b configuration using doppler tracking : 11 evla antennas were available for these observations .",
    "unfortunately , we discovered that doppler tracking with the evla antennas produced large phase jumps between the targets and calibrators for all but one source ( g11.92@xmath220.61 ) for which the sky frequency of the target and calibrator were sufficiently close to permit calibration ( this problem has since been fixed ) .",
    "for the other sources the phase stability was sufficiently good during the short observations that maser emission could be detected in uncalibrated vector - averaged u - v plots ( it is notable that weak masers or masers far from the phase center would not have been apparent in these plots ) .",
    "the 18 uncalibratable sources with maser features apparent in the original _ u - v _ data were reobserved at 6.7 ghz in february 2008 in fixed - frequency mode ; the larger overheads associated with fixed - frequency observing did not permit reobserving all 28 sources in the allotted time .",
    "the fixed - frequency 6.7 ghz evla observations were obtained on 2008 february 1 in the b configuration and 2008 february 9 , 17 , and 19 in the cnb configuration : 13 evla antennas were available for these observations .",
    "the sources were split into two groups based on their declinations , and each group of sources was observed twice .",
    "the bandwidth was 1.56 mhz ( 70 km  s@xmath5 ) ; aliasing on evla - evla baselines using the interim system ( evla antennas and vla correlator ) meant that the usable bandwidth was @xmath130 km  s@xmath5 .",
    "the aliasing is worse for narrow bandwidths and in the presence of broadband continuum emission .",
    "the spectral resolution was 3.05 khz ( 0.14 km  s@xmath5 ) , prior to offline hanning smoothing .",
    "the data were taken in single polarization mode .",
    "for each source , the phase calibrator , bandpass calibrator , flux calibrator , observation date , velocity range searched for maser emission , and synthesized beam size are listed in table  [ 67obstable ] .",
    "our 44 ghz vla observations , of the 18 egos observed with fixed frequency at 6.7 ghz plus g11.92@xmath220.61 , were obtained on 2008 february 16 and 18 in the cnb configuration , in fixed frequency mode : 26 antennas were available for these observations .",
    "one if was tuned to the 44.069410 ghz ch@xmath0oh ( 7@xmath20 - 6@xmath19 )   a@xmath4 ( @xmath21=62.9 k ) maser transition ; the bandwidth was 3.125 mhz ( 21 km  s@xmath5 , @xmath119 km  s@xmath5 usable due to the aliasing described above ) and the spectral resolution 24.4 khz ( 0.17 km  s@xmath5 ) , prior to offline hanning smoothing .",
    "pseudo - continuum observations were obtained simultaneously ( @xmath23=44.1 ghz , 25 mhz bandwidth divided into 16 channels ) .",
    "the data were taken in single polarization mode .",
    "the bandpass calibrator was j2253 + 161 and the flux calibrator was 3c286 .",
    "fast switching was used with a cycle time of 2 minutes , and the pointing model was updated once per hour during the observations . for each source , the phase calibrator , observation date , velocity range searched for maser emission , synthesized beam size , and continuum rms from the wideband data are listed in table  [ 44obstable ] .    in the calibration of both the 6.7 ghz and 44 ghz datasets ,",
    "a model was used for 3c286 .",
    "all maser data were self - calibrated using the channel with the strongest maser emission ( except for the g37.48@xmath220.10 44 ghz data , which did not have sufficiently strong masers ) .",
    "we estimate that the absolute flux calibration is accurate to @xmath110% , and that the absolute positional uncertainty is @xmath101 .",
    "our vla observations were obtained prior to the single dish molecular line observations of our ego sample described in  [ jcmtobs ] .",
    "source velocities for tuning the vla correlator were obtained from a broad range of data from archives and the literature . as subsequent followup shows , this was not always ideal ( see  [ results ] ) . the primary beam ( fwhp ) of the vla is 67 at 6.7 ghz and 10 at 44 ghz .    the search for maser emission in the 6.7 and 44 ghz image cubes was automated using the aips task sad .",
    "these data are dynamic range limited such that the rms noise in channels with bright maser emission is significantly increased compared to non - maser channels ( this is due primarily to relatively poor _ u - v _ coverage ) . to account for this limitation ,",
    "the rms noise cutoff for sad was adjusted from a conservative value of @xmath24 for the majority of the channels in each cube to as high as @xmath110@xmath25 for those channels containing strong emission .",
    "this was a greater issue for the 6.7 ghz data than the 44 ghz data because the former had significantly fewer operational antennas .",
    "tables  [ 67obstable ] and [ 44obstable ] list the minimum , maximum , and median threshold values used for each source . only spectral features above these thresholds in at least two channels are reported .",
    "the median 6@xmath6 detection limit for the whole sample of 19 egos is @xmath10.16 jy ( brightness temperature t@xmath26@xmath11247 k ) for the 6.7 ghz data and @xmath10.15 jy ( t@xmath26@xmath1330 k ) for the 44 ghz data .",
    "reported maser flux densities and intensities have been corrected for primary beam attenuation .",
    "observations of hco@xmath4(__j__=3 - 2 ) and h@xmath27co@xmath4(__j__=3 - 2 ) were obtained at the james clerk maxwell telescope ( jcmt ) on 2008 may 28 - 30 towards 18 of the egos surveyed for ch@xmath0oh masers with the vla ( g10.34@xmath220.14 excepted ) .",
    "two 1 ghz ifs were observed simultaneously : one if was centered on hco@xmath4(__j__=3 - 2 ) at 267.558 ghz ( @xmath21=12.8 k ) in the usb , while the other if covered h@xmath27co@xmath4(__j__=3 - 2 ) at 260.255 ghz ( @xmath21=12.5 k ) in the lsb .",
    "also included in the h@xmath27co@xmath4 tuning was the ch@xmath0oh(5@xmath28 - 4@xmath29 ) transition at 266.838 ghz ( @xmath21=44.3 k ) in the usb .",
    "position - switching mode was used , with each ego observed for 3.5 minutes on - source .",
    "in addition , a subset of 10 egos was observed in position - switching mode with a single , 1 ghz if centered on sio ( 5 - 4 ) at 217.105 ghz ( @xmath21=20.8 k ) in the lsb : 8 sources were observed during the 2008 may 28 - 30 observing run , and one source each on 2008 june 12 and 13 .",
    "the egos in the sio subsample were chosen to have associated 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers and strong , broad hco@xmath4 line wings .",
    "integration times for the sio observations were adjusted based on weather and source elevation and ranged from 10 to 15 minutes on - source .",
    "the `` off '' positions were chosen to avoid irdcs and msfrs , using 8 and 24 @xmath2 m _ spitzer _ images ; the angular separation between the `` off '' and target position ranged from @xmath13 - 7 .",
    "we did not perform dedicated observations to check the off positions for emission ; however , no evidence for emission in the off beam is seen in the h@xmath27co@xmath4 spectra .",
    "the spectral resolution was @xmath1488 khz for both observing setups , corresponding to a velocity resolution of @xmath10.55 km  s@xmath5 for the hco@xmath4 observations and @xmath10.67 km  s@xmath5 for the sio observations .",
    "the sio spectra were subsequently smoothed to a resolution of 1.5 km  s@xmath5 to increase their signal - to - noise .",
    "the data were obtained using the a3 receiver and the acsis digital autocorrelation spectrometer , and reduced using the starlink software package .",
    "line - free regions near each line of interest were selected for baseline - fitting , and a linear baseline was removed from each spectrum .    the observation dates , rms , and fitted line properties for each source are listed in table  [ jcmtfitstable ] . during the 2008 may run ,",

    "the detection rate of 6.7 ghz class ii ch@xmath0oh masers towards egos in our survey is at least 64% : of the 28 sources in our original sample , 18 have maser emission coincident with the ego .",
    "this detection rate is a lower limit because vector - averaged _ u - v _ plots select for strong masers near the phase center ( see  [ vlaobs ] ) : the 9 sources that were not reobserved could have weak 6.7 ghz masers .",
    "including the three egos not targeted but observed serendipitiously ( see  [ results ] ) , the detection rate is essentially the same ( 20/31 , @xmath15 64.5% ) .",
    "the masers range in strength from @xmath10.5 to 469.4 jy  beam@xmath5 ( t@xmath26@xmath17390 to 1743038 k , see table  [ maserfitparams_67 ] ) .",
    "this detection rate for 6.7 ghz masers towards egos is considerably higher than those of single - dish surveys with comparable sensitivity ( rms @xmath16 0.3 jy ) towards _ iras _ or water maser selected samples , which are @xmath137% and 35% , respectively @xcite .",
    "the detection rate toward egos is also much higher than for a single - dish survey of glimpse point sources selected on the basis of 8 @xmath2 m intensity and [ 3.6]-[4.5 ] colors , which is less than 20% @xcite .",
    "the detection rate of 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers towards egos in our survey is @xmath190% ( 17/19 ) .",

    "h@xmath7o and 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , both established tracers of massive star formation , have been detected previously in the vicinity of some of the egos in our sample , either through blind surveys or targeted searches of nearby msfrs ( see table  [ samplelit ] ) .",
    "however , most of the previous data are from single dish telescopes , and consequently have relatively poor angular resolution ( 07 - 7 for ch@xmath0oh and 07 - 19 for h@xmath7o ) .",
    "this resolution makes it difficult to establish a physical association between an ego and a maser reported in the literature .",
    "table  [ samplelit ] presents a list of all the possible associations that we have found , though there are a number of caveats .",
    "for example , the spectrum of the 6.7 ghz maser g24.93 + 0.08 ( * ? ? ?",
    "* a blind survey with 55 resolution and 30@xmath10 positional accuracy ) is a blend of two masers resolved by our vla observations ( g24.943 + 0.074 , coincident with the ego g24.94 + 0.07 , and g24.920 + 0.088 ) , and the published position is @xmath11 from the ego .",
    "the position for g35.03 + 0.35 from @xcite , the single - dish survey with the highest angular resolution ( 07 ; a blind survey with 7@xmath10 pointing rms ) , is offset from 4.5 and 24 @xmath2 m emission and is 13@xmath10 from our interferometric position .",
    "the h@xmath7o maser surveys generally have smaller beams , but target maser and _ iras _ positions that are themselves uncertain .",
    "only three targeted egos ( g11.92@xmath220.61 , g23.01@xmath220.41 , g35.03 + 0.35 ) are definitely associated with known h@xmath7o masers ( maser positions known to @xmath81@xmath10 from interferometric observations , see table  [ samplelit ] ) .    in addition to the targeted egos with possible 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser associations from single dish observations ( table 4 ) , we reobserved 8 egos with previous interferometric detections of 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers to obtain improved sensitivity and positional accuracy .",
    "our sample includes 5 egos with 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser detections in the @xcite australia telescope compact array ( atca ) survey , and one ego ( g11.92@xmath220.62 ) that fell within the field of view of that survey but was not detected .",

    "the nominal detection limit of the @xcite survey ( 0.5 jy ) is about three times poorer than that of our vla observations ( 0.16 jy ) , but these authors targeted _ iras _ sources ( 04 to 22 from our ego targets ) , reducing the sensitivity at the ego positions ( atca primary beam @xmath185 fwhp at 6.7 ghz ) . in all cases , we detect maser emission over a wider velocity range than reported by @xcite , and our positions differ by up to 18 ( for the weak maser associated g28.28@xmath220.36 at -03@xmath36 declination ) .",
    "we also detect two weak ( @xmath161.1 jy  beam@xmath5 ) 6.7 ghz maser spots towards g11.92@xmath220.61 (  [ g1192 ] ) , which were undetected by @xcite .",
    "since the kinematics of 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission are of interest for understanding the nature of egos , we also reobserved three sources for which only positions and peak velocities were reported by @xcite ( and references therein ) .      while detection rates for both 6.7 ghz class ii and 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers are very high towards the egos in our survey ,",
    "the spatial distributions of the two maser types are quite different . figure  [ 3color ] illustrates several general , salient points : ( a ) 6.7 ghz class ii ch@xmath0oh masers are spatially concentrated , typically within one synthesized beam ( @xmath12@xmath10 ) , ( b ) 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers are usually , but not invariably , coincident with discrete 24 @xmath2 m sources , ( c ) each ego is usually associated with only one ( at most two ) locus of 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission , ( d ) 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers are spatially distributed , often across many tens of arcseconds ( 10@xmath10@xmath10.2pc at a typical distance of 4 kpc ) , ( e ) most egos are associated with two to many tens of locii of 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission , and ( f ) many 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers are coincident with extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission ( seen as green in figure  [ 3color ] ) or appear to trace edges where extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission meets the surrounding environment ( e.g. an irdc ) .",
    "a corollary is that the positions of 6.7 and 44 ghz masers are , in general , anticorrelated : 6.7 ghz masers are centrally concentrated , towards 24 @xmath2 m sources , while 44 ghz masers are distributed across ( and in some cases , beyond ) the area of extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission .",
    "these general statements are discussed in more detail below and in  [ individualsources ] .",
    "each diamond plotted in figure  [ 3color ] represents the fitted position of a 6.7 ghz maser in a single velocity channel .",
    "although in general there are many diamonds plotted for each source in figure  [ 3color ] , they tend to overlap at the sizescale of these images into one or a few maser groups .",
    "to account for this we have two approaches : ( 1 ) each cluster of masers ( typically at different velocities ) that lie within a synthesized beam ( @xmath12@xmath10 , see table  [ 67obstable ] ) is defined as a `` maser group '' , with its position defined by the intensity weighted mean ( table  [ 67iweighted_egos ] ) ; and ( 2 ) the fitted position of each maser spot is reported in table  [ maserfitparams_67 ] .",
    "the sub - synthesized - beam kinematic analysis facilitated by these fits will be discussed in  [ maserkin ] and  [ individualsources ] . for each ego in our survey within the fwhp of the vla primary beam at 6.7 ghz ( 67 ; 19 targeted egos plus 3 serendipitiously observed ) , table  [ 67iweighted_egos ] lists the properties of associated 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser group(s ) and the angular separation of the 6.7 ghz maser group(s ) and 24 @xmath2 m ego counterpart .",
    "only two egos are potentially associated with multiple 6.7 ghz maser groups : g11.92@xmath220.61 and g49.42 + 0.33 .",
    "the case of g49.42 + 0.33 is ambiguous : two spatially and kinematically distinct maser spots are detected , separated by @xmath19@xmath10 ( @xmath10.5 pc at 12.3 kpc , see also  [ g4942 ] ) . the western maser spot ( g49.416 + 0.326 )",
    "is associated with the ego , but lacks a discrete 24 @xmath2 m counterpart ; however , g49.42 + 0.33 is much more distant than the other egos in our sample , so the sensitivity of the mipsgal survey corresponds to an intrinsically brighter 24 @xmath2 m upper limit .",
    "the eastern maser spot ( g49.417 + 0.324 ) is associated with a 24 @xmath2 m source , but may not be associated with the ego .",
    "table  [ 67iweighted_egos ] quantifies the correlation of 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers and 24 @xmath2 m emission that is visually apparent in figure  [ 3color ] . excluding the ambiguous case of g49.42 + 0.33 , of the 21 remaining egos in table  [ 67iweighted_egos ] ( 18 targeted plus 3 serendipitously observed ) , 2",
    "do not have 6.7 ghz maser detections ( g49.27@xmath220.34 and g49.27@xmath220.32 ) and 2 do not have discrete 24 @xmath2 m counterparts ( g10.29@xmath220.13 and g28.28@xmath220.36 ) . of the remainder , the angular separation between a 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser and the nearest 24 @xmath2 m counterpart is @xmath161@xmath10 for 13/17 egos ( 76% ) , and @xmath163@xmath10 for all sources with 24 @xmath2 m detections .",
    "@xcite characterize the absolute positional accuracy of the mipsgal survey by cross - correlating sources in 8 @xmath2 m glimpse and 24 @xmath2 m mipsgal images and examining the distribution of positional offsets .",
    "the tail of the distribution extends up to 3@xmath10 , with the median offset being 085 .",
    "the larger maser-24 @xmath2 m angular separations ( @xmath12 - 3@xmath10 ) that we find in regions where the 24 @xmath2 m emission is saturated and/or likely consists of blended contributions from several sources ( g11.92@xmath220.61 , g19.36@xmath220.03 , g35.03 + 0.35 ) are consistent with the greater uncertainties in attempting to measure positions in such regions . with the exception of the two sources identified without discrete 24 @xmath2 m ego counterparts ( g10.29@xmath220.13 , g28.28@xmath220.36 ) and the ambiguous case of g49.42 + 0.33 , the positions of 24 @xmath2 m ego counterparts and 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers from our survey are coincident within the combined uncertainties of the mipsgal absolute astrometry @xcite and our measurements of the 24 @xmath2 m source positions ( see note ( a ) to table  [ mipstable ] ) .",
    "as shown in figure  [ 3color ] , there is diversity in the relationship of 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers to extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission . as for the 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , each individual magenta cross plotted",
    "represents a fitted position of a 44 ghz maser in a single velocity channel .",
    "details of the 44 ghz maser kinematics are discussed in  [ maserkin ] and  [ individualsources ] . in stark contrast to the class ii 6.7 ghz masers , the class i 44 ghz masers are , in general , widely distributed over tens of arcseconds .",
    "of the 17 egos with 44 ghz maser emission , only one is associated with a single locus of maser emission .",
    "for the majority of sources , the distribution of maser emission is spatially and kinematically complex , and not well characterized as an ensemble of mean `` spots '' ( in contrast to the 6.7 ghz masers discussed above ) .",
    "a striking feature of the images in figure  [ 3color ] is that many sources ( @xmath31/3 ) exhibit filamentary arcs of 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission ( e.g. g11.92@xmath220.61 , g19.01@xmath220.03 , g19.36@xmath220.03 , g22.04 + 0.22 , g24.94 + 0.07 , g35.03 + 0.35 ) . in these sources ,",
    "the maser arcs appear to trace out the edges of 4.5 @xmath2 m arcs or lobes .",
    "similarly , in g28.83@xmath220.25 , 44 ghz masers are concentrated near the edges of the extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission , though the masers themselves do not trace out an arc .",
    "some 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers are apparently dissociated from any obvious mir emission ( e.g. the masers in irdcs , offset from egos , in the g18.89@xmath220.47 and g28.83@xmath220.25 fields ) .",

    "massive stars form in clusters , however , surrounded both by other massive objects and by intermediate and low mass stars , raising the question of whether different sources might be responsible for the 6.7 and 44 ghz maser emission .",
    "as discussed in  [ spatial44 ] and  [ individualsources ] , there are examples of far - flung 44 ghz masers that may be excited by sources other than the ego . in general , however , the 4.5 @xmath2 m morphology shown in fig .",
    "[ 3color ] argues that the same source  a myso  is reponsible for exciting both the 6.7 ghz class ii ch@xmath0oh maser emission ( by heating its surrounding environment ) and at least some of the 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh maser emission ( by driving an outflow ) .",
    "g19.01@xmath220.03 is a particularly suggestive example : two bipolar lobes of 4.5 @xmath2 m emission , coincident with arcs of 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , emanate from a 24 @xmath2 m point source coincident with a 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser .",
    "the results discussed above are strong evidence that the egos in our survey sample are young mysos that are actively driving outflows , and hence actively accreting .",
    "while our sample was selected to cover a range of mir properties , it included only egos categorized as `` likely '' myso outflow candidates by @xcite , and the sample of egos searched for 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission was , in essence , a 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser - selected ego subsample .",
    "further studies are required to establish whether _ all _ egos are mysos with active outflows , and particularly whether the distinction between `` possible '' and `` likely '' outflow candidates drawn by @xcite based on mir morphology is borne out by observations of other outflow tracers .",
    "the kinematics of the ch@xmath0oh masers , while revealing for individual sources , exhibit such diversity across our sample that they allow few generalizations about egos as a population , beyond the observation that 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers are generally at or near the thermal gas @xmath37 .",
    "this is consistent with the excitation of maser emission at the interface with surrounding dense ambient gas : for a kinetic temperature of 80 k , @xcite found that maser emission in the 44 ghz transition is strongest at densities of @xmath110@xmath11 - 10@xmath66 @xmath12(n(h@xmath7 ) ) .",
    "it is also consistent with the sketch of @xcite for class i ch@xmath0oh masers excited in a shell behind the shock front for outflows in the plane of the sky  an orientation preferentially selected for by the @xcite criterion of extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission .",
    "as noted above , the sample of egos searched for 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission was essentially a 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser - selected subsample .",
    "class i 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission was detected towards @xmath189% ( 16/18 ) of egos with 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , as well as towards the one targeted ego without an associated 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser .",

    "the two 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser groups in g11.92@xmath220.61 are separated by @xmath11.6 km  s@xmath5 in velocity and @xmath144 ( @xmath317000 au at 3.8 kpc ) and may be tracing two distinct protostars , a possibility that exists for other sources in our survey .",
    "the evolutionary sequence of a forming massive star may be broadly described , following the terminology of @xcite , as a progression from a cold dense massive core ( cdmc ) to a hot dense massive core ( hdmc ) to a disk - accreting main - sequence star ( dams ) to the final main - sequence star ( fims ) , where the transition from a hdmc to a dams occurs when the central , accreting source becomes powered more by hydrogen burning than by disk accretion .",
    "refining this sequence and adding physical detail requires being able to establish the relative ages of large samples of mysos on the basis of observational evidence .",
    "while _ spitzer _",
    "surveys have provided large samples , the use of broadband mir data for this purpose is complicated by the fact that multiple molecular , ionic , and pah lines fall within each of the irac bands ( c.f .",
    "fig . 1 of * ? ? ?",
    "* ) , and evolutionary models that include all these emission mechanisms in realistic geometries are not yet available . at longer wavelengths ( e.g. mips 24 @xmath2 m ) , the broadband flux is more likely to be dominated by thermal dust emission .",
    "@xcite has argued that such thermal emission may emanate from heated dust in the walls of an outflow cavity ( as opposed to pinpointing the protostar itself ) , and the point in the evolutionary sequence , relative to other indicators , at which 24 @xmath2 m emission becomes observable is not well characterized as a function of viewing angle or protostellar mass . for our ego sample , the detection of thermal emission in the ch@xmath0oh   ( 5@xmath28 - 4@xmath29 ) transition ( @xmath21=44.3 k ) toward the majority of sources in our jcmt survey is suggestive of possible hot core line emission ( e.g. * ? ? ?",
    "* ) , but followup with a more diverse range of organic tracers is required .",
    "two more established observational indicators of evolutionary state are masers and hii   regions , although both remain imperfectly understood . @xcite propose a `` straw man '' evolutionary sequence in which a forming myso first excites class i ch@xmath0oh masers ( via a protostellar outflow ) , then class ii ch@xmath0oh masers ( radiatively pumped by photons emitted by warm dust ) , then h@xmath7o masers ( associated with outflows ) , and finally oh masers ( radiatively pumped by fir photons ) and uc hii   regions in quick succession .",
    "each of these stages overlaps with those before and after , and @xcite note that there are sources known to be inconsistent with this sequence .",
    "most egos in our sample are associated with both class i and class ii ch@xmath0oh masers , placing them early in the @xcite evolutionary sequence .",
    "some class i ch@xmath0oh masers detected in our survey  which are apparently isolated from mir emission or class ii ch@xmath0oh masers  may be excited by outflows from even younger protostars , or from ysos not massive enough to excite 6.7 ghz class ii ch@xmath0oh maser emission .",
    "the egos in our sample have not been systematically searched for h@xmath7o or oh masers at high angular resolution .",
    "three sources ( g11.92@xmath220.62 , g23.01@xmath220.41 , g35.03 + 0.35 ) are known to also have associated h@xmath7o masers ; of these , two ( g23.01@xmath220.41 , g35.03 + 0.35 ) also have oh masers coincident with the ego @xcite .",
    "these egos may thus either be examples of sources inconsistent with the @xcite sequence , or in fact be protoclusters , with ysos at different evolutionary stages responsible for different types of maser emission .    while it is generally accepted that uc hii   regions represent a late stage of massive star formation ( the end state ( fims ) in the sequence of * ?",

    ", cm wavelength continuum emission has been detected coincident with mir emission towards two egos in our sample ( g35.03 + 0.35 and g49.27@xmath220.34 , see also table  [ samplelit ] ) , but the existing data are insufficient to establish the nature of this emission . at 44 ghz , both thermal emission from dust and free - free emission from ionized gas may contribute to the continuum ; without multiwavelength observations , these can not be disentangled . the non - detections ( 18/19,@xmath195% ) of 44 ghz continuum emission coincident with egos in our survey are consistent with other evidence ( masers , mir properties ,  [ discussion_natureofegos ] ) that egos are young mysos .",
    "given the depth of our survey , however , the non - detections do not provide strong constraints on the properties ( luminosity , mass , ionizing photon flux , spectral type ) of the `` central '' sources responsible for powering the outflows traced by 4.5 @xmath2 m and class i ch@xmath0oh maser emission . at a typical distance of 4 kpc",
    ", an unresolved 5@xmath6 detection would correspond to an ionizing photon flux of @xmath19.4@xmath3210@xmath70 photons@xmath5 ( following * ? ? ? * and assuming a typical electron temperature of 10@xmath65 k ) , equivalent to a single star cooler than spectral type b1.5 @xcite .",
    "this estimate gives a _ lower limit _ for the ionizing flux that corresponds to our detection threshold , as it assumes that every ionizing photon emitted produces observable free - free radiation ( e.g. that quenching and absorption by dust are both unimportant ) .",
    "it also assumes optically thin free - free emission @xcite ; in the case of optically thick free - free emission , derived parameters dependent on the electron density ( including the ionizing photon flux ) will be underestimated ( c.f . discussion in * ? ? ?",
    "* ) . under similar assumptions , the photon flux of 10@xmath70 photons@xmath5 assumed by @xcite in modeling very young",
    "ionized accretion flows around forming mysos would be below our detection limit . extrapolating the peak 15 ghz ( 2 cm ) intensities for uc hii   regions in the survey of @xcite ( kcw94 ) to 44 ghz assuming optically thin free - free emission ( s@xmath710.1 ) , only @xmath150% of the kcw94 uc hii   regions would be detected at the 5@xmath6 level ( @xmath15 mjy  beam@xmath5 ) in our survey .",
    "the 15 ghz observations have approximately the same resolution as our 44 ghz observations and kcw94 sources with s@xmath72,peak(15 ghz)@xmath9s@xmath72,peak(8.4 ghz ) ( inconsistent with optically thin free - free emission ) were excluded .",
    "the overwhelming lack of 44 ghz continuum detections of egos in our survey thus serves to rule out bright uc hii   regions as powering sources in most cases , but deeper observations are required to constrain the presence of fainter uc or of hc hii   regions .",
    "smaller and denser than uc hii   regions , most hc hii   regions have rising spectral indices ( @xmath73@xmath11 ) at cm - mm wavelengths and are generally faint ( @xmath16 10 mjy ) even at 44 ghz @xcite .",
    "emission from mysos attributed to ionized stellar winds is likewise faint at 44 ghz ( 5/8 sources in the sample of * ? ? ? * with peak intensity @xmath85 mjy  beam@xmath5 ) .",
    "sensitive , high angular resolution observations over a range of cm wavelengths are required to further constrain the presence , extent , and physical properties of any ionized gas associated with egos .",
    "the results of our vla and jcmt surveys constitute a preponderance of evidence that egos are young mysos with active outflows :    * class ii 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , which are associated exclusively with mysos , are detected towards @xmath364% of egos surveyed ( 18/28)nearly double the rate of surveys using other myso selection criteria .",
    "* class i 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , which trace molecular outflows , are detected towards @xmath190% of egos surveyed ( 17/19 ) and @xmath189% ( 16/18 ) of egos with associated 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers .",
    "* @xmath38v@xmath39 in the hco@xmath4(3 - 2 ) line is @xmath320 km  s@xmath5 for the majority of egos surveyed , consistent with the presence of outflows .",
    "* sio(5 - 4 ) emission , which is predicted to persist for only @xmath110@xmath65 years after the passage of a shock , is detected towards 90% ( 9/10 ) of egos surveyed  a rate comparable to that of sources with narrowband h@xmath7 emission believed to be excited by outflow shocks . * thermal ch@xmath0oh   ( 5@xmath28 - 4@xmath29 ) emission , indicative of the presence of warm dense gas , is detected toward 83% ( 15/18 ) of egos surveyed . *",
    "no 44 ghz continuum emission is detected at the 5 mjy level ( 5@xmath6 ) toward @xmath195% of egos surveyed ( 18/19 ) , ruling out bright uc hii   regions as powering sources .",
    "class ii 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission is spatially concentrated in compact maser groups ( extent @xmath161@xmath10 ) , which are generally coincident with 24 @xmath2 m emission .",
    "each ego is associated with only one or two 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser groups .",
    "class i 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser emission , in contrast , is generally widely distributed over many tens of arcseconds , coincident with extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission . hco@xmath4(3 - 2 ) emission is detected towards all egos surveyed ( 19/19 ) ; the profiles are characterized by broad line wings , consistent with the presence of outflows .",
    "in addition , all surveyed egos ( 19/19 ) are detected in h@xmath27co@xmath4(3 - 2 ) emission , allowing the determination of revised kinematic distances based on the new galactic rotation model of @xcite .",
    "thermal ch@xmath0oh(5@xmath28 - 4@xmath29 ) emission is also detected towards the majority of egos in our sample ( @xmath183% , 15/18 ) , at the same velocity as the h@xmath27co@xmath4(3 - 2 ) emission ( median velocity offset @xmath160.3 km  s@xmath5 ) .",
    "these results verify that egos are a promising sample for studying accretion and outflow at the early stages of massive star formation .",
    "there is also evidence that two of the egos surveyed may in fact be protoclusters of at least two mysos , providing opportunities to study how myso outflows interact in the dense environments characteristic of most msf .",
    "the next steps are to establish the nature of the driving sources .",
    "deep cm continuum observations will more strictly constrain the presence or absence of ionized gas ( and hence ionizing photons ) .",
    "high angular resolution ( sub)mm line and continuum observations will constrain the physical properties ( temperature , density , mass ) and numbers of compact cores .",
    "high angular resolution observations in direct molecular outflow tracers are also required to better characterize outflow kinematics and energetics : 44 ghz class i ch@xmath0oh masers are a strong indicator of the presence of a molecular outflow , but are preferentially excited near the systemic velocity and provide no information about outflow mass or momentum .",
    "these projects are well matched with the capabilities of the evla and alma , and egos will be promising targets for these facilities .    this research has made use of nasa s astrophysics data system bibliographic services and the simbad database operated at cds , strasbourg , france .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> we present the results of a high angular resolution very large array ( vla ) class i 44 ghz and class ii 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh maser survey of a sample of @xmath120 massive young stellar object ( myso ) outflow candidates selected on the basis of extended 4.5 @xmath2 m emission in _ spitzer </S>",
    "<S> _ galactic legacy infrared mid - plane survey extraordinaire ( glimpse ) images . </S>",
    "<S> these 4.5 @xmath2m - selected candidates are referred to as extended green objects ( egos ) , for the common coding of this band as green in three - color irac images . </S>",
    "<S> the detection rate of 6.7 ghz class ii ch@xmath0oh masers , which are associated exclusively with massive ysos , towards egos is @xmath364%nearly double the detection rate of surveys using other myso selection criteria . the detection rate of class i 44 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers , which trace molecular outflows , is @xmath189% towards egos associated with 6.7 ghz ch@xmath0oh masers . </S>",
    "<S> the two types of ch@xmath0oh masers exhibit different spatial distributions : 6.7 ghz masers are centrally concentrated and usually coincide with 24 @xmath2 m emission , while 44 ghz masers are widely distributed and generally trace diffuse 4.5 @xmath2 m features . </S>",
    "<S> we also present results of a complementary james clerk maxwell telescope ( jcmt ) single - pointing molecular line survey of egos in the outflow tracers hco@xmath4(3 - 2 ) and sio(5 - 4 ) . </S>",
    "<S> the hco@xmath4 line profiles and high sio detection rate ( 90% ) are indicative of the presence of active outflows </S>",
    "<S> . no 44 ghz continuum emission is detected at the 5 mjy  beam@xmath5 ( 5@xmath6 ) level towards 95% of egos surveyed , excluding bright ultracompact hii   regions as powering sources for the 4.5 @xmath2 m outflows . </S>",
    "<S> the results of our surveys constitute strong evidence that egos are young , massive ysos , with active outflows , presumably powered by ongoing accretion . </S>"
  ]
